<div id="review_1891694077" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1891694077" />
    <a title="Elena" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7779073-elena"><img alt="Elena" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1329485169p2/7779073.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1891694077?book_show_action=true">Jan 27, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Elena" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Elena" href="/user/show/7779073-elena">Elena</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7779073-elena?shelf=2017-book-challenge-120">2017-book-challenge-120</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1891694077" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4754725369163824174">Overall - I liked this one due to a great idea behind an intricate mystery plot! However, it kept somewhat falling flat ... The romance part of the book was also lacking, as the main couple got very little "screen time" together... They were mostly apart, so i found it hard to believe in this love that was developing between them. Therefore, this novel - which had SO much potential - let me down on both levels > with the mystery AND with the romance! If only one of the two were written a bit bet</span>
  <span id="freeText4754725369163824174" style="display:none">Overall - I liked this one due to a great idea behind an intricate mystery plot! However, it kept somewhat falling flat ... The romance part of the book was also lacking, as the main couple got very little "screen time" together... They were mostly apart, so i found it hard to believe in this love that was developing between them. Therefore, this novel - which had SO much potential - let me down on both levels &gt; with the mystery AND with the romance! If only one of the two were written a bit better, this would be a 4* read, easily! <br><br>My biggest issue while reading this book - especially at the beginning - was that I had mixed feelings as to what the author was trying to say and accomplish. The beginning was written in a confusing way and felt like parts of the story were randomly missing. I'm assuming the author did it for some sort of effect, but a lot of the story was just unclear and I wasn't able to connect with the characters until much later, due to this! <br><br><u>1st example of confusing writing/missing parts:</u> <br>At the beginning, Hunter (poker player and playboy) is at his friend's whorehouse and is approached by Priscilla, a porn star, (why?! how?! do they already know each other?!) and he rejects her - even though it is hinted at them having had some sort of relationship... He then hires a whore, has sex with her and passes out ... In the morning - the whore has disappeared... But not much attention is paid to this at that point. Then we have a flash forward to Hunter throwing a house party for the rich and famous - enter Elizabeth. Here we find out that Elizabeth's had a crush on him since she was a teenager... During this party, she is snooping through his house, only to witness him having, what is hinted at being rough bdsm, sex with Priscilla. The reader is now left confused - what is he doing with the porn star, when he showed no interest in her in the last chapter? How long ago was that brothel scene when he rejected her? Last night? Few nights ago? Months? Years? The timeline here is completely unclear... To make things even weirder - Hunter catches Elizabeth spying on him , kicks Priscilla out and goes down on Elizabeth ... I mean - ew - he just had sex with someone else!!! <br><br><u>2nd example of confusing writing:</u><br>Elizabeth's best friend, Cross, ends up in an accident-induced coma. His rich-as-sin parents refuse to pay for his care (WTF?! WHY?!) and Elizabeth has to sell her virginity at the brothel in order for Cross to get the care he needs. Really? Of all these insanely rich people, only poor Elizabeth thinks that she should be paying for his care?! Literally, the ONLY person without money is the person offering to pay?! What about their mutual friend, Suri, who has a CRUSH on Cross?! She wears a multi-million dollar ring on her finger, yet she can't offer to pay for her crush's care?! Made NO sense! <br><br><u>3rd example of missing parts of the story:</u><br>Hunter has a dark secret from his childhood - Rita, his stepmother <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ was in some way abusive to him. "Slapping around" was mentioned, but never the context or the reason! So we never really know what was the issue between them. So when the big "reveal" comes - that at some point he hit her back and the fall killed her - I didn't really know what to feel! Did he just kill his stepmom for no reason?! Did he kill her in self-defence?! I mean - an older woman smacking him around, does NOT justify a 16-year-old guy hitting her back so hard that she falls and splits her head open! Were there no other options for him ?! Was it more than smacking him around? Was she fully abusive even while he was a small child?! <i>WHY</i> was she abusive and in what way?! We don't know ANY of this!  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br><u>4th example of confusing plot/missing parts of the story:</u><br><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[<br>At some point, we finally find out that Hunter thinks that Priscilla is trying to frame him for the disappearance of the whore from the brothel, so THAT's WHY he engages in a sexual relationship with her, even though he doesn't want her... He acts as if he is appalled and repulsed, yet he allows her to whip him and do all kinds of nasty and hurtful things to him. Is this really necessary?! Just because you think she's trying to frame you, you will let her beat you, whip you, and humiliate you - how is this helping you solve the case ?!?! <br>Finally, the person who Priscilla is working with is revealed - and we find out about their human trafficking plot - selling whores to Mexican drug lords, who in-turn, sell these women further into slavery ... Yet we never find out how Priscilla (and the politician she works with) picked out Hunter to be their scapegoat?! Why him?! How did they even know him / of him - a poker player ?! Also, we find out that this politician and Priscilla caused Cross's accident (i.e. tried to kill him) - why?!?!?!?! What did Cross have to do with anything?! He was just Elizabeth's friend - he did not even know Hunter... weird!  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br>The ending was also very haphazard - everything finishes off in a few rushed , action-filled pages, without too many details or even much of an explanation. The explanation that is offered is overly simplified and does not really clarify such an intricate white-slavery plot that was laid out earlier... <br><br>So overall - lots of dark topics touched upon, lots of suspense and mystery, but everything seemed a bit (pardon my language) half-assed! It seemed like the author had a lot of good things going, but only touched upon each and then let them be! <b>Not one thing</b> was worked out thoroughly! That's what I call a waste of great potential! <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1456776295ra/18275805.gif" width="350" height="350" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>
  <a data-text-id="4754725369163824174" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

Without proper care after his parents write him off, Lizzy decides to cash in her V-card to the highest bidder…<br/><br/>“’We’ll put you up on billboards around Vegas and we’ll talk you up. Something like…</span>
  <span id="freeText2549341085863519610" style="display:none">I have never had this much trouble writing a review before...*frustrated*<br /><br /><br />“Holy crap. Holy insanity. Holy vagina.” <br />--Ella James, Selling Scarlett <br /><br />Bottle water heiress, Elizabeth (Liz, Lizzy, Libby) DeVille is a virgin. It doesn’t seem like a big deal until an accident leaves her friend, Cross, in a coma. Without proper care after his parents write him off, Lizzy decides to cash in her V-card to the highest bidder…<br /><br />“’We’ll put you up on billboards around Vegas and we’ll talk you up. Something like…’Selling Scarlett’.” “And I’m Scarlett?” “Yeah. You like it?” I’m not sure how I feel about it, but I say, “Yeah. Scarlett sounds good.”’” <br /><br />Whiskey heir, professional poker player, and playboy, Hunter West doesn’t do relationships. With a complicated past, it just seems easier to pay for his affections. Hunter is a regular at Vegas brothel, Love Incorporated, owned by his long-time best friend, Marchant Radcliffe. Hunter enjoys his “no strings attached” lifestyle until a devious (and in my opinion, crazy) Priscilla Heat decides to use him in ways no one thought possible. Next thing he knows, Hunter wakes up after a night with one of his favorite escorts, to a massive hangover and a missing girl…with him being the main suspect. Keeping his distance from Vegas and Love, Inc. seems like the best thing until he finds out about “Scarlett.”<br /><br />Ah, the plot thickens…<br /><br />“’This is good for you,’ he tells me. “Real good. You got a price I wouldn't dream of and the bidder is a good guy. That’s a Disney ending.’”<br /><br />Or is it? <br /><br />This book has so much more to it than just what the title indicates. There are sub-plots, a plethora of characters, and a constant change of POV from Elizabeth to Hunter (which I actually enjoyed—it’s like getting both sides of the story at once). This tale is a tangled web of secrets, lies, lust, sex, politics, crime, addiction, money, abandonment, resolution, friendship, trust, and ultimately, love. At the beginning, I was confused and overwhelmed by all of the descriptive wording used by the author, sometimes it was a bit too much but the story-line held true and the ride Ms. James took me on was definitely a memorable one. I look forward to the next installment of Love, Inc.<br /><br />**Four Heated Stars**<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="2549341085863519610" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/594961605" />
    <a title="Amanda" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/16642053-amanda"><img alt="Amanda" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1442647983p2/16642053.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/594961605?book_show_action=true">Apr 19, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Amanda" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Amanda" href="/user/show/16642053-amanda">Amanda</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/17379508-selling-scarlett">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer594961605" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1017565604956038449">Selling Scarlett by Ella James<br/>Review done by Amanda <3<br/><br/>If you're like me, this book was a breath of fresh air. I was in a funk. A serious book funk. Everything I read wasn't doing it for me. I was about to get professional help when Ella James stated she was releasing Selling Scarlett last Friday. I had read the blurb before and I was so excited. Finally something different had come a long. Then amazon made me wait. For three effing days. I was seriously upset. But I finally woke up one day and i</span>
  <span id="freeText1017565604956038449" style="display:none">Selling Scarlett by Ella James<br />Review done by Amanda &lt;3<br /><br />If you're like me, this book was a breath of fresh air. I was in a funk. A serious book funk. Everything I read wasn't doing it for me. I was about to get professional help when Ella James stated she was releasing Selling Scarlett last Friday. I had read the blurb before and I was so excited. Finally something different had come a long. Then amazon made me wait. For three effing days. I was seriously upset. But I finally woke up one day and it was live. I bought and went on a ride. A gritty erotic ride. I have read James's other series and was not expecting the sex to be so detailed and hawt! I have to say this author has definitely crossed the YA line and did it very well. Lizzy or as Hunter calls her Libby, was strong and willing to do anything for her friend. She just didn't expect for Hunter to be her savior. I didn't realize that this was going to be a suspense and it sure left me on the end of my seat. Biting my nails and pulling on my hair. The story kind of left me crazy. The most interesting thing about this book is the way James paints the escorts. You don't stop to think that they have lives or even why they are escorts to begin with. It actually made me love them just as much as Lizzy and Hunter. Now Hunter knows how to pull some heart strings. I never cry during reading but I shed a few for him. I have a similar past and it certainly made me connect with him. Lizzy also has a bad past and she is independent and strong because of it. Their relationship is a slow sweaty hot build. I found myself panting and swooning. I love that they didn't automatically end up in bed. In fact it was near the end before the really hot stuff happened. Now I didn't like everyone. Priscilla can die and rot in hell. She seriously upset me. So did Lockwood. James really did a good job with making you hate the villains. I also wasn't fond of Cross but he grew on me and I'm excited to see what happens in his book! 5 huge stars! Well written and beautiful. Gritty and heart stopping. Selling Scarlett is a must read!</span>
  <a data-text-id="1017565604956038449" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer14497833928520421072">Okay let me start out by saying Ella James you are freaking INCREDIBLE I mean Holy Shiz this series started out with a bang and I could not get enough. The cast of characters made this book incredible and the flow of it had me on the edge of my seat ready to come apart because I was like what the heck is going on.   <span id="freeText14497833928520421072" style="display:none">Okay let me start out by saying Ella James you are freaking INCREDIBLE I mean Holy Shiz this series started out with a bang and I could not get enough. The cast of characters made this book incredible and the flow of it had me on the edge of my seat ready to come apart because I was like what the heck is going on. I thought it was going one way but then totally went the other way.<br /><br />Elizabeth aka Scarlett is a loyal and devoted daughter and best friend. She will do anything to help out her mother and best friend Cross. When Cross is in an accident and needs help she comes up with a plan to help him out. The plan at first had me cracking up until I realized she was serious as all hell. The plan is to auction off her Virginity. Crazy you say well that is what I thought at first but then as I was reading more and more I realized she loves Cross and does not want to see him suffer. So as a great friend she will do whatever it is to help him. <br /><br />What she does not take into the equation is Hunter Hot As Hell West. She has crushed on him for forever but he is dark and mysterious and always aloof so she crushes on him hard and when she decides to auction herself and finds herself in the hands of her crush she is both terrified and excited. The only thing standing in her way is Hunter himself. See Hunter has secrets very very dark fifty shades of fucked up secrets and he does not want her to know. But Scarlett is determined to break the barriers and find out what he is into and give herself to him. See Hunter loves gambling and prostitutes. He is mixed into some serious shit and when shit hits the fan it really hits. But Scarlett is determined to get Hunter. Will she have him in the end? Can she break through his barriers and show him they can be together? Well you have to read it to find out!</span>

    <a title="Stina Rubio" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6780913-stina-rubio"><img alt="Stina Rubio" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1448672975p2/6780913.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/594998406?book_show_action=true">Apr 19, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Stina Rubio" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Stina Rubio" href="/user/show/6780913-stina-rubio">Stina Rubio</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/17379508-selling-scarlett">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6780913-stina-rubio?shelf=indie-authors">indie-authors</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6780913-stina-rubio?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6780913-stina-rubio?shelf=romance">romance</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer594998406" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15861932560407989427">I had wanted to read this book when I see how beautiful this cover was. I didn't even read the blurb. I seen banners posted that it was going to be on sell for the first couple days--and that sold me. I waited, not so patiently biting my nails in anticipation. I didn't know what to expect I didn't read the blurb until I actually bought the book. I dove into waters that were not clear and uncharted, and I am sure once you start to read this book it will become clear that it is a fantastic new con</span>
  <span id="freeText15861932560407989427" style="display:none">I had wanted to read this book when I see how beautiful this cover was. I didn't even read the blurb. I seen banners posted that it was going to be on sell for the first couple days--and that sold me. I waited, not so patiently biting my nails in anticipation. I didn't know what to expect I didn't read the blurb until I actually bought the book. I dove into waters that were not clear and uncharted, and I am sure once you start to read this book it will become clear that it is a fantastic new concept for a book. Maybe there is more out there like it but I haven't ever read something like this before. Selling Scarlett was amazing and engaging. It made me cry, it made me laugh, and at times I was sitting on the edge of my seat wondering what was going to happen next. It had a bitch for a villain, and a heroine that will have you rooting for her the whole time. Let me not forget about Hunter, good God, hunter!!!! Swooning isn't even the word I would use to describe what this character did to my insides. He was, so, so sexy. Having issues from his past Hunter needed to work things out in his life, it made you want to help him.<br /><br />A story like this doesn't come alone often and when it does you just need to sink your teeth into it and hold on for the ride of you life. Ella James spun a mesmerizing tale, one that people will be talking about for years to come. I enjoyed this book immensely, and it will be one I will re-read over and over again. </span>
  <a data-text-id="15861932560407989427" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('kl+eGXaKa//7q4tEb4cxZS4pdGbuWuN+UT4fGAbF23aQDqDOyGz04ETeAMGnPsM2Eq/XZ+wL/GrglMTFKyBMhQ==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }
